Grand Ceremony for Confucius's Ritual in Qufu 107

Representatives Pay Respects at Confucius' Tomb

Jinan Correspondence: After the restoration of the Confucius ritual, this year the National Government dispatched representatives to Qufu to pay respects and visit the tomb for the first time. The ceremony was extremely grand. Central National Government representatives Chu Minyi and Ye Chucang, etc., arrived in Qufu from Beijing on the 26th and returned to Yanzhou that evening. At 5:00 a.m. on the 27th, they returned to Qufu by car to hold the ceremony. The details are recorded as follows:

Ritual Music and Instruments 108

In front of the statue of the First Teacher in the Dacheng Hall were displayed the following: in the front row were the Bian and Dou sacrificial vessels, followed by the Tailao, then the Five Offerings, and finally the Ten Offerings. All were Zhou Dynasty sacrificial instruments, including the Zhou Kui Feng Dou, Zhou Bao Fu, Zhou Bo Yi, Zhou Xi Zun, Zhou Ya Zun, Zhou Tao Yan, Zhou Pan Kui Dun, Zhou Four-Legged Li, Zhou Ce You, and Zhou Wood Ding. Next were the Five Styles. Ye Chucang presented a pair of wreaths inscribed "In Memory of the Birthday of the First Teacher Confucius," signed "Respectfully presented by Ye Chucang, Special Envoy of the National Government." In front were sandalwood censers. Eight rows of dancers were set up on the platform outside the hall, with sixty-four musicians and dancers in charge of their respective duties. Ancient music was displayed outside the hall, including the ancient Te Qing, golden bells and jade chimes, Bo Zhong, Zu Gu, Tian Gu, Tao Gu, and Bo Fu Gu, one of each; six qin and four se. There were also two Hui flags and one Wu Tong each. The dance flute had more than twenty sections. The two officiating personnel were dressed in purple flower ritual robes with black-edged square scarves and hats. The Hui flags were divided into two types: the ascending dragon flag was used to start the music, and the descending dragon flag and the Wu Tong were used to stop the music. However, only a few instruments could be played, such as the Zhong Lu, Qin Se, Zhu Fou, etc., which no one could play anymore, and were almost extinct.

Ceremony Order 109

One table was set up on the east and one on the west outside the hall. The eulogy was placed on the west table and read by Chai Zuxin, section chief of the Military Affairs Office. The master of ceremonies was Fu Xuanqing, chief of the first section of the Military Affairs Office. Song Jintang, clerk of the Bureau of Ceremonies of the Military Affairs Office, and staff member Zeng Beixing, were in charge of the ceremony. The musical instruments and dancers faced south on the stage. Ye Chucang, the chief officiant, was in the front, followed by the accompanying officiants, representatives of various ministries and departments, the heads of the provincial Department of Civil Affairs and Education, the participating officiants, and the Qufu County Magistrate. All wore blue gowns. Male guests were on the east side and female guests on the west side, watching on both sides. The descendants of Confucius were east of the apricot altar, and the Confucius Association was behind them. Various Qufu groups, schools, and institutions were west of the apricot altar.

National Ritual Ceremony 110

The ceremony began at seven o'clock. The chief officiant, accompanying officiants, participating officiants, and officiating personnel went to the front of the hall in sequence and lined up according to the designated order. Music was played, the national anthem was sung, wreaths were presented, the eulogy was read, three bows were performed, music was played, and one more bow was performed. They retreated and the ceremony was completed. On that day, the government sent about four hundred people, including the chief officiant, accompanying officiants, guests, etc. The order was solemn and dignified. About four or five thousand people watched freely. The public ceremony ended at 7:20.

Confucius' Family's Words of Thanks 111

After the representatives paid their respects, Kong Decheng, the Duke Yansheng, gave a written speech of thanks. The original text reads: "Decheng is now deeply grateful to the National Government's Five Yuans and various ministries, the Shandong Provincial Government, the heads of the Departments of Civil Affairs and Education, and all the officials who have come from afar to pay respects. The doctrines of the First Sage have been popular for more than two thousand years and are known to all, both ancient and modern, Chinese and foreign. Decheng dares not boast. Since the founding of the Republic of China, there have been internal troubles and external threats, and wars have been frequent. The ceremony of respecting the First Sage has not been held. Today, I am honored by the presence of all the officials in Qufu. I think that Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Three Principles of the People quote the First Sage a great deal, which is to respect the First Sage. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek promotes the New Life Movement and emphasizes the old morality, which is to respect the First Sage. Chairman Han Fuju has also proposed repairing the Confucius Temple, which is to respect the First Sage. In the future, there will be harmony and admiration both at home and abroad. I congratulate the future of the Republic of China, and I congratulate the National Government and the Provincial Government."

Confucius Family Ritual 112

After the public ceremony, the family ritual was held, presided over by Kong Decheng, the 77th generation descendant of Confucius. The rest of the family members stood on both sides of the central aisle of the incense burner in front of the apricot altar. The musicians and dancers held shields and feathers in the center of the platform. There were four masters of ceremonies, one inside and one outside the hall, and one in front of the apricot altar. The ceremony was as follows: 1. Offering incense, 2. First offering, 3. Offering silk, 4. Reading the eulogy, 5. Second offering, 6. Drinking blessing wine, 7. Bestowing honor. During the ceremony, they first kowtowed nine times in front of the apricot altar, then ascended the steps to the hall on the west side and kowtowed nine times, offered incense, and kowtowed nine times again, then returned to their original positions. Music was played for each ritual. The family ritual ended at ten o'clock.

Visit to the Tomb 113

After the ceremony, they took cars to Confucius' Tomb. At twelve o'clock, the tomb visiting ceremony was held. Eight dishes were placed on the stone table at Confucius' tomb. Military music was played, and Ye Chucang presided over the ceremony. The order was as follows: stand at attention, sing the national anthem, present wreaths, perform three bows, play music, perform one bow, retreat, ceremony completed, take photos. The representatives then toured the vicinity of the tomb for a while before returning to the Confucius Mansion by car.

Kong Decheng Speaks 114

The current Duke Yansheng Kong Decheng is the 77th generation descendant of Confucius. He is fifteen years old and extremely intelligent. It is said that his family is currently managed by his aunt. He has two elder sisters, one married to Ke Yanling in Beiping and one married to the son of Feng Shu. He has finished reading the Four Books and is currently studying the Confucian Classics, and also learning arithmetic, history, geography, and other subjects.

Confucius Mansion Banquet 115

The Confucius Mansion held a banquet to entertain guests from all over. Kong Decheng hosted a separate banquet for representatives from the Central Government and the Provincial Government. During the banquet, Kong Lingcan, a representative of the Kong family (Chief of the First Section of the Education Department), reported the difficulties of the Confucius Mansion to Vice Minister of the Interior Fu Rulin. Initially, Confucius' sacrificial land was 100,000 hectares, but now most of it does not pay rent. He requested that it be restored in order to honor the sacrificial rituals. Fu agreed to find a way to maintain it and asked the Confucius Mansion to send a detailed list of the land to the ministry for verification.

Confucius Mansion Garden 116

The residence of the Duke Yansheng, called the Duke's Mansion, occupies a large area. Many close relatives of the Kong family live here. Due to the recent decline in the Kong family's fortunes, the Duke's Mansion has been unable to make ends meet and its debts have been increasing. This national ritual held by the Central Government was unexpected by the Kong family and was considered a great honor. According to the Kong family, the iron tree in the Duke's Mansion garden suddenly bloomed this year, and the lights in front of the Duke's Mansion suddenly became bright, which is a sign of the revival of Confucianism. Because this year's events were rushed, not many Kong family members came from various places. It is expected that the number will increase next year. The garden behind the Duke's Mansion is elegantly decorated, with artificial mountains, pavilions, pools, and many flowers and trees, all of which are ancient. There are more than ten pots of cacti, as tall as a person, and there are also iron magnetic seedlings. After the representatives finished the ceremony at the Confucius Temple, they returned to the Duke's Mansion to rest, and Kong Decheng and the Duke's Mansion receptionists led them to visit the garden and took several motion pictures.

Departure from Qufu 117

After the representatives finished their meals, they returned to Yanzhou by car. Kong Decheng presented calligraphy scrolls, literature examination papers, and Han and Wei stone tablets to the representatives. The Confucius Association presented the Records of Respect for Confucius Through the Ages. After the representatives arrived in Yanzhou, they rested at the Railway Hotel. At 3:00 p.m., Ye Chucang, Chu Minyi, Fu Rulin, and others returned to Nanjing. The rest of the staff, along with Li Shuchun, took a special train to Taian at 4:10 to climb Mount Tai. The group included representatives from the Legislative Yuan Peng Yangguang, the Judicial Yuan Chen Gemin, the Examination Yuan Lin Xiang and Wang Yongbin, the Ministry of Education Cao Zhen, Secretary Wang Yizhi, Section Chief Zhang Daichun, Medical Officer Lei Chengjie, Clerk Xu Chunzhi, and Clerk Zhao Quan. They stayed in Taian that night and climbed the mountain the next day. (27th Night)

Plainclothes Troops Discovered in Yutian, Hebei Province 118

More than a Hundred People with Complete Firearms

Authorities Pay Attention to Prevention

Tianjin Correspondence: The Yutian Security Team's commander, the issue of the team's reduction to a thousand men, and all disputes in the war zone must wait for Huang Fu to return and negotiate with the Japanese side, so they cannot be resolved immediately. Before these issues are resolved, it was suddenly reported that plainclothes troops were discovered near Tuanshanzi in Yutian. According to inquiries, on the 24th of this month, several hundred troops suddenly appeared between Fengrun, Jixian, and Zunhua counties, occupying villages. They claimed that they were not bandits, but plainclothes troops under the command of a certain unofficial military figure. People saw that the team's firearms were well-equipped and dared not neglect it, so they were prepared to treat them with courtesy. The matter was heard by the commander of the Third Battalion of the Security Team stationed in Jixian County, who rushed to lead his troops there. However, the team claiming to be plainclothes troops fled without a trace upon hearing the news. The next morning, more than a hundred so-called plainclothes troops also appeared in Wangtian Tuanshanzi, dressed in disheveled clothes, but all were fully equipped with firearms. They hid in the mountains, planning to do something. On the same day, Yin Rugeng happened to come to Tianjin to visit Yu Xuezhong to request instructions on the takeover of Majiagao and road construction in the war zone. He received a report from the Yutian County Magistrate and immediately went to the Provincial Government to report to Yu. Yu immediately telegraphed the Yutian Security Team to take strict precautions. However, after the telegram was sent, the province was not sure whether the Security Team would follow the order. Therefore, it also telegraphed the neighboring Jixian, Zunhua, and Fengrun counties to step up their precautions. As of today, there has been no news, so it is thought that the plainclothes troops, seeing that there was no opportunity to take advantage of, have turned to other places. On the day that plainclothes troops were discovered in Yutian, a disheveled team also appeared in the San Nü'er River in Fengrun County, numbering about eighty. They claimed to be subordinates of Liu Zuozhou, of the First General Team of the Security Forces in the war zone stationed in Luanxian County, and were ordered to go out to suppress bandits. The team had more than fifty large guns and more than ten pistols, and the rest were unarmed. Although the San Nü'er River Police Station suspected the team, they did not dare to act rashly. On the one hand, they looked for lodgings and provided food and drink, and on the other hand, they secretly reported to the County Government. After the County Government forwarded the report to Liu Zuozhou's headquarters in Luanxian County, they received a reply stating that no team had been sent out to suppress bandits. County Magistrate Zhang Renli immediately secretly ordered the San Nü'er River Police Station to find a way to confiscate the firearms of the bandit team. The police, due to their small numbers, planned to use persuasive methods to make the team abandon their weapons and flee. The bandits refused to listen and retreated to Zhangzhuangzi, where they relied on the terrain to confront the police. A fierce battle broke out that day. County Magistrate Zhang Renli received the news and led the police team to assist on the evening of the 25th. After a half-day of fierce fighting, the bandits were defeated and scattered in all directions. It is said that the bandits were also plainclothes troops ordered to operate in Fengrun. The source of these plainclothes troops is said to be that Shi Yousan recently went to Changchun to ask the Japanese and puppet sides to give him a title so that he could operate in North China. The Japanese side, seeing that all recent negotiations had been successful and that everything in North China could be taken at will, refused the request because they felt that there was no need to organize a group for Shi Yousan. Shi returned to Tianjin disgruntled and recruited Ma Henggui, who was hiding in the puppet capital (Ma was the leader of the plainclothes troops in the former Tianjin Incident), and recruited the remaining troops of Zhang Haipeng's army in Rehe along the Great Wall line to form plainclothes troops in the war zone, planning to cause disturbances. Therefore, the authorities are paying close attention to this and are urgently seeking ways to prevent it. (26th)

Severe Drought in Zhejiang Province Causes Water Transportation to be Cut Off: The Image Shows the Dry Riverbed and Cracked Bottom at the Steamer Wharf in the North Gate of Haining County

Xiang, Guangdong, and Guangxi Armies Surround and Suppress the Xiao Bandits 119

Xiao Ke Plans to Flee from Western Hunan into Sichuan and Guizhou

Under the Pursuit of the Large Army, He is Already Heavily Besieged

Changsha Correspondence: The bandits being suppressed by the Western Route Army were originally the troops of Kong Hechong, Gao Yongsheng, Cai Huiwen, Yu Xingzhou, Xiao Ke, etc., with Xiao's troops being the most fierce. For more than a year, the Western Route Army has successively broken through the bandit nests in western Jiangxi, and completely recovered the counties occupied by the bandits. The various troops of Kong, Gao, Cai, and Yu have all been successively eliminated. Only Xiao Ke's pseudo-Eighteenth Division remains, hiding in Faxin Mountain in Yongxin. The unit is surrounded and suppressed by the *Number Removed* Column, causing the bandit area to gradually shrink, with the aim of annihilating them. Because Xiao's bandits were blocked and could not survive, they detoured out of Suichuan through mountain roads, taking advantage of the situation to invade southern Hunan, passing through Rucheng, Guidong, Zixing, Xintian, Guiyang, and other counties, and reaching Yongzhou. The journey took only a week, with daily rapid marches of more than a hundred *li*, specifically detouring along small roads to avoid contact with the army corps. Currently, Xiao's bandits number about ten thousand, with three to four thousand guns, and have gathered on the east bank of the Xiang River and Xiao River, between Lingling, Qiyang, Xintian, and other counties, attempting to cross the west bank, go out of Wubao, pass through western Hunan, and enter Sichuan and Guizhou to join forces with He Long's bandits. The armies of the three provinces of Hunan, Guangdong, and Guangxi have gathered on the west bank of the Xiang River and are divided into three parts: "pursuit," "blockade," and "interception," advancing towards the bandits at the same time. Xiao's bandits are indeed trapped in an important encirclement, and it is expected that the armies from all sides will reach the concentration point within three or four days, and will immediately launch a fierce attack on Xiao's bandits. (26th)

Anhui Province Handling Famine Relief 120

Borrowing Funds from Banking Circles to Stabilize Grain Prices

Sending Personnel to Purchase Drought-Resistant Seeds

Anqing Correspondence: Since the flood in Anhui Province in the 20th year of the Republic, the rural economy has collapsed, and households have few savings. This summer's unusual drought has caused a disaster, and the people are feeling particularly difficult to obtain food. The Department of Construction has recently received representatives from various counties, requesting relief. The Department stated that the government is already planning as a whole, and local areas should also urgently seek self-help, and instructed them to pay attention to this. However, the representatives all stated that they were planning to urgently stabilize grain prices, but it was difficult to raise funds, and requested that the Department introduce them to banks for loans. The Department then sent Secretary Fang Junqiang to contact various banks. Most of the bank managers were away on other business, so he consulted with Zhou, the manager of the Anqing branch of the Shanghai Commercial Bank. According to his proposal: (1) The use of the loan is limited to stabilizing grain prices; (2) For every 10,000 yuan borrowed, the local area must also raise 2,000 yuan on its own to combine with the grain, in order to offset losses. If they want to borrow more, the same principle applies; (3) The income and expenditure of stabilizing grain prices will be supervised by personnel sent by the bank; (4) No collateral is required; (5) The loan interest rate and repayment period will be decided by the head office. The representatives from various counties also believe that this is fair and sufficient to stabilize grain prices and provide famine relief. Currently, the bank has requested instructions from its Shanghai head office, and it can be decided and implemented within a few days. However, the Department of Construction believes that the disaster area this year is too wide and there are many starving people. Stabilizing grain prices is only one of various relief measures, and it is not possible to rely solely on its success. It is necessary to also plan other forms of assistance. Yesterday, it specially telegraphed the Provincial Government, requesting that it forward the matter to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, and promptly instruct the Farmers Bank of the Four Provinces to refer to the agreed-upon proposal and allocate loans to meet urgent needs. The Department also believes that the drought area in Anhui Province has reached 48 counties, so it has made repeated efforts in water diversion projects to provide irrigation, and has supervised various counties to quickly purchase drought-resistant and short-term crop seeds such as buckwheat, green beans, and turnips, and distribute them to disaster-stricken farmers for timely planting. It has also sent technicians to Shanghai, Wuxi, Suzhou, Changzhou, Bengbu, and Congyang to purchase more than 10,000 yuan worth of seeds such as buckwheat, potatoes, turnips, and rapeseed, and has telegraphed various counties to prepare the price and send personnel to collect them to supplement the shortage. All counties north of the Anhui River are designated to collect them from Bengbu, and counties in central and southern Anhui are designated to collect them from Anqing and Wuhu, respectively. As of recently, the number of seeds requested by various counties is as follows: more than 2,600 *shi* of buckwheat, more than 200 *shi* of potatoes, more than 40 *shi* of turnips, and more than 20 *shi* of rapeseed. The amount of seeds that have been successively distributed is as follows: more than 400 *shi* of buckwheat and 300 *shi* of potatoes. The rest will be distributed after the purchased seeds are transported. It has already telegraphed the various purchasing committees to purchase them day and night and distribute them separately, and to complete this by the end of the month. At the same time, it has stipulated the methods for various counties to distribute seeds and has compiled methods for planting potatoes, strictly ordering them to follow the guidance, in order to provide some relief to the disaster-stricken farmers in the drought area. (August 27)

Wuxi 125

River Water is Cut Off and There are Few Measures to Save the Drought

The section of the river from Qinglong Bridge on East Street to Wubu Bridge on West Street in Zhangjingqiao, District 6, has long been cut off, and river traffic has also been cut off as a result. Fortunately, there are still few fields in the middle, so it has little impact on irrigation. Although the river water has not been cut off in the nearby Northeast Tang area, the river water in Chenjiaqiao, Huangtutang, and other places has also been cut off, so the water source for the farmland in the Northeast Tang area has also been cut off at both ends. Although there are water-scooping boats, they cannot do anything. If it does not rain, the rice will definitely dry up and die. The township chiefs and local people in the two places have repeatedly held meetings to discuss the matter, but because of a lack of funds, they have not been implemented. They can only watch the rice dry and die.

This year's drought has caused the mulberry leaves to wither, which has a significant impact on autumn sericulture. The county's sericulture model area was originally allocated 230,000 sheets of autumn silkworm eggs by the Department of Construction, but now only more than 110,000 sheets have been determined. According to the budget, this is only half of the original amount. Therefore, the Department of Construction has specially telegraphed various districts to reduce and consolidate the guidance centers established according to the original plan. After receiving the order, Cai Jingde, the Deputy Director of the county's sericulture model area, went to the province yesterday to visit Director Shen to ask for instructions on everything. He returned to Wuxi that night. According to reports, the county has already decided on the principle of reducing and consolidating, but how to start the reduction and consolidation depends on the local situation in each village. In addition, the county's Silkworm Seed Trade Association held a meeting yesterday and resolved to ask the Department of Construction to pay the price of non-acid-treated silkworm eggs immediately, and appointed Jiang Jiayou and Hou Shuzhi as representatives to go to the province to petition.

The fare for the entire Zhenjiang-Danyang section is 48 cents. The bus terminal in Danyang is at the city gate, and the terminal in Zhenjiang is at the Zhongshan Bridge. Passengers can save on rickshaw fares. In terms of time, the bus only takes forty minutes, the same as a special express train.

City News, The City Received Showers Yesterday 135

Rice Prices Gradually Decline

According to the Central News Agency, the rice produced this year in various regions has been affected by drought, resulting in reduced harvests. People are deeply concerned about food. However, local governments are now making every effort to seek relief. In addition, there has been timely rainfall in various regions, so rice prices have eased slightly.

Showers Yesterday 136

Starting at 12:30 PM yesterday, the city experienced showers. Although it was not long, Jiangwan and other places in the city received more rain and for a longer period. As these areas are mostly farmland, it will be of great benefit to the crops. Therefore, yesterday's rice prices were even lower than the previous day. According to the astronomical observatory, there will be more showers in the next few days.

Four Provinces Purchase Rice 137

According to investigations by reporters with relevant parties, except for Hunan and Anhui provinces, which are self-sufficient, other provinces such as Hubei, Zhejiang, Jiangsu, and Jiangxi need to rely on external sources. Jiangxi Province, in particular, needs more rice due to the presence of large troops for bandit suppression. However, the authorities in Jiangxi have already purchased and stockpiled a large amount of rice, so there may be no panic for the time being. The authorities in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Hubei provinces are planning to negotiate with the banking sector to regulate food supply through loans or investments. The Zhejiang authorities plan to purchase rice from Wenzhou and Taizhou in southern Zhejiang, where there was a good harvest this year. If this is not enough, they will purchase from Fujian, as Fujian also had a good harvest this year. Hubei and Jiangsu provinces plan to purchase foreign rice. The banking sector is said to be very sympathetic to this matter, and there should be no problems.

Rice Prices Will Not Rise Again 138

According to those familiar with the conditions in various rice-producing areas, the drought this year is not as severe as rumored. Moreover, there has been timely rainfall in the Yangtze River basin, which is beneficial to the autumn harvest. Therefore, rice prices have begun to decline. In this city, the market price the other day fell by four or five jiao. If the rain continues, prices may not exceed the authorities' price limit.

Sha Hansheng Discusses the Current Situation of Overseas Chinese in Brazil 139

Going to Beijing This Morning to Report to the Central Government

According to the Central News Agency, Sha Hansheng, Secretary of the Chinese Embassy in Brazil and Standing Committee Member of the Kuomintang Branch in Brazil, arrived in Shanghai on the German ship "Fu Er Te" on the 26th to report on the recent situation of overseas Chinese affairs and party affairs in Brazil. He is scheduled to go to Beijing on the morning of the 30th to report to the Central Party Headquarters and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited him at his residence yesterday morning. According to his discussion, the situation of overseas Chinese in Brazil is as follows:

Over a Thousand Overseas Chinese 140

According to Sha, there are more than 1,300 overseas Chinese in Brazil, mostly from Guangdong and Zhejiang provinces. The Cantonese overseas Chinese are mostly laborers, such as those working in restaurants and laundries. They have a significant influence in the labor community in northern Brazil. The Zhejiang overseas Chinese are mostly merchants, selling goods such as porcelain and embroidery. The cost of living in Brazil is relatively low, so they are still relatively affluent. However, the amount they can remit back to China is very small because the value of Brazilian currency is lower than that of any other country.

Party Affairs Progress 141

The Kuomintang in Brazil only had a liaison office in the Brazilian capital before 1932 due to various reasons. After 1932, it was changed to the Kuomintang branch in Brazil. Since then, party affairs have gradually progressed. In November of last year, it was changed to the Kuomintang Branch directly under the Central Government in Brazil. It has spared no effort in promoting party affairs, so there are already more than 200 official party members. Among the remaining overseas Chinese, 80 to 90 percent are probationary party members who can all believe in and practice the Three Principles of the People.

Sino-Brazilian Trade 142

Regarding trade between China and Brazil, the main Chinese goods shipped to Brazil in recent years are tea and porcelain. However, the operators are not Chinese, but foreigners. The business situation is also deteriorating year by year. This is because Brazil is strongly promoting its own goods within the country, and they are very cheap. Foreign goods entering the country are subject to restrictions, so business is declining day by day. The Brazilian government provides strong protection for the safety of overseas Chinese and there have been no anti-Chinese incidents, so overseas Chinese can live and work in peace.

Supplementary Chinese Language Lessons 143

Most of the overseas Chinese in Brazil go there as adults, and most are from the working class. Therefore, few have studied Chinese characters. Some are illiterate and cannot communicate. Therefore, the Kuomintang Branch directly under the Central Government in Brazil and the Chinese Association have established supplementary schools at night. The results have been good since their establishment. Sha continued to say that there are many children of overseas Chinese in Brazil, but there are no formal Chinese schools, which is a cause for concern.

Going to Beijing This Morning 144

Sha finally stated that he has lived in Brazil for more than ten years and has not returned to China for a long time, so he has requested a four-month leave to return to China. In addition to inspecting the situation in China, he also needs to report on the situation of party affairs and overseas Chinese affairs in Brazil to the Central Party Headquarters and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. He is scheduled to take the early train to Beijing tomorrow morning (today). As for Xiong Chongzhi, the Chinese Minister to Brazil, he has not indicated that he will return to China.

Customs Administration Ordered the Customs to Release the Detained Zhang Rice Yesterday 147

The Grain Association Submitted a Letter of Guarantee

According to the Shin Shih News Agency, about 30,000 bags of Zhang rice, transported to Shanghai by Xiamen rice merchants, have been offered to various parties for sale in Shanghai. Customs officials, suspecting that Fujian Province was not a rice-producing area, questioned where such a large amount of rice came from and ordered its detention for inspection. After half a month of negotiations, Shen Shuyu, the Director of the Customs Administration, ordered the Customs to release the rice yesterday. The details are as follows:

Zhang Rice Detained in Shanghai 148

Zhangzhou has a large amount of rice, which has never been sold in Shanghai because it was needed by the province. Since the taxation of foreign rice last year, domestic rice has sold well and is easier to sell than before. Xiamen rice merchants purchased a large amount of new rice from Zhangzhou when it came on the market and transported it to Shanghai for trial sales. On the 2nd of this month, 130 bags were shipped to Shanghai by 16 Xiamen rice shops, including De Tai, Jin Rui, Hui Long, and Fu Yuan. Subsequently, several thousand bags were shipped by boat. However, this Zhang rice was collected from the countryside, and the quality and color were not uniform. Shanghai rice merchants had never seen it before. At a time when various provinces were suffering from drought and demand was high, the first several thousand bags were sold out, with substantial profits. Therefore, Xiamen was telegraphed to continue shipping rice to Shanghai. Unexpectedly, the rice was suspected by customs officials and detained for inspection. Seven or eight ships en route were detained one after another, totaling more than 30,000 bags. All were temporarily stored in customs warehouses and not released.

Customs Inspection Difficult to Decide 149

After detaining the rice, the Customs collected various types of domestic and foreign rice from the Grain Association for comparison and research. It also submitted it to the Tax Commissioner of the Verification Office for testing by experts in the chemical testing room, but without any results. It also ordered the Xiamen Customs to investigate the Zhang rice producing area and submit samples for detailed investigation. The Xiamen Customs samples arrived on the 26th and were compared and tested by experts. The composition of the rice was similar in various places, with no significant difference. It could not be determined whether it was foreign rice. Finally, Bode, the Customs Commissioner of the Jianghai Customs, submitted a request to the Inspector General of Customs, Bland, for a final decision. After careful comparison and research, Bland felt that although the rice could not be determined to be foreign rice, it had a significant difference in color, size, and pointiness from the rice produced in Rangoon, Saigon, Taiwan, Korea, and Japan. However, because rumors were rife and there were reports of mixing it with domestic rice, he could not make an immediate decision on how to resolve the matter.

Association Guarantees Release 150

Many parties proved that the Zhang rice should be released, such as the Xiamen Chamber of Commerce, Hong Kong rice merchants, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the Shanghai Grain Association, and the Zhangquan Association. They sent letters and telegrams to the Jianghai Customs to prove it. The Xiamen Customs also sent personnel to conduct an on-site investigation and telegraphed the Customs to prove its release. Yesterday, the Grain Association also sent personnel to the Customs Administration to petition. Director Shen Shuyu was in Shanghai and listened to the petitioners present the details of the situation. He also stated that the new Zhangzhou rice had a high moisture content and would ferment and rot if stored in customs warehouses for a long time. He asked for consideration for the merchants' blood money. After listening to the petition, Director Shen immediately called Bland of the Review and Verification Department and asked him to release the rice immediately if there was no sufficient evidence. After receiving the call, Bland telegraphed the Jianghai Customs to allow the release, but for the sake of caution, the Grain Association was asked to prepare a formal guarantee letter, stating that if it was later found that there was indeed a mixture, the Association would be responsible. The case of detaining the rice, which had been entangled for more than a month, was thus resolved.

Imports of Foreign Rice Increased Sharply in July 151

Totaling More Than 3.82 Million Yuan

Most Imports Came From Annam and Siam

This year's floods and droughts have resulted in a sharp decline in harvests. Rice merchants, seeing the potential for profit, have ordered foreign rice in large quantities, resulting in a sharp increase in imports. A reporter from the Xin Xin News Agency investigated the International Trade Bureau yesterday and learned that the total imports of foreign rice in July amounted to more than 3.82 million yuan, several times higher than the imports in the same month in previous years. Most imports came from Annam and Siam. The import quantities and countries are listed below: Siam 225,736 metric tons, Annam 164,896 metric tons, India 70,632 metric tons, Singapore 1,510 metric tons. According to the declared import prices, the total is more than 3.82 million yuan.

Zhejiang Provincial Government Borrows Money to Help Silkworm Farmers 152

Autumn Cocoons Are Reeled, Spun, and Woven

Contacting Tianzhang Factory to Weave Silk

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the silk industry in China has declined, and silk factories have closed down, greatly affecting the livelihood of farmers. The Zhejiang Provincial Department of Construction borrowed money from the banking sector to handle autumn silkworm affairs. A reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency met with Chu Huiseng, the leader of Zhejiang silk merchants, yesterday and learned that the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Construction, in addition to distributing autumn silkworm eggs to farmers, decided to organize cocoon collection agencies to reel the collected cocoons into raw silk, and contacted the Hangzhou Tianzhang Silk Factory to weave the silk into fabric, and then find ways to sell it. The Central Government Approved Jiangsu Province to Issue 20 Million Yuan in Public Bonds 154

To Consolidate Old Debt Surplus

To Complete the Huai River Diversion Project

According to Shin Shih News Agency, the Jiangsu Provincial Government decided to issue 30 million yuan in public bonds to develop water conservancy and consolidate old and new debts. It had previously drafted measures and detailed rules and submitted them to the Central Government for approval. The Central Government initially thought that Jiangsu Province had suffered from disasters for years, the market was depressed, and the people were in difficulty, so it planned to reduce the amount of this public bond to 10 million yuan. However, the Jiangsu Provincial Government believed that the established plans were all in urgent need of implementation and could not be reduced further, so it sent the Directors of the Department of Finance and the Department of Civil Affairs to Beijing to explain. As a result, a compromise was reached to allow the issuance of 20 million yuan, which was formally approved by the Central Political Conference yesterday. After being transferred to the Executive Yuan for approval, it can be transferred to the Jiangsu Provincial Government for issuance.

Most of it Will Be Used to Consolidate Old Debts 155

The original purpose of this Jiangsu Province's issuance of public bonds was to (1) consolidate old debts of various banks, (2) complete the Huai River Diversion Project, and (3) dredge the new Grand Canal. Now that the originally planned amount has been reduced, the allocation of funds must be slightly changed. According to a reporter's investigation with the Jiangsu Bank, the issuance of this new public bond will be used primarily to repay the old debts of the banking sector. The old debts of the banks in Jiangsu that need to be consolidated amount to about 6 million yuan, with deed tax revenue as collateral. At the same time, there are also 9 million yuan of construction bonds issued in the past, with salt tax surcharges as collateral. The issuance of the above-mentioned public bonds was not formally approved by the Central Government, so it is also necessary to consolidate them urgently.

Only 5 Million for Water Conservancy Development 156

Therefore, after the issuance of 20 million yuan in public bonds, 15 million yuan will be transferred to the relevant banks as repayment of the principal and interest of old debts and old public bonds. After the old debts are repaid, the deed tax and salt tax surcharge, which are the collateral for the old debts, will be transferred to the new public bonds to serve as a fund for repayment of principal and payment of interest. The annual income from the deed tax is 1 million yuan, and the annual salt tax surcharge is about 1.8 million yuan, which is more than enough to cover the annual principal and interest of the new debt. The annual interest rate of the new debt has been set at 7 percent, with a term of 20 years. The remaining 5 million yuan will be used to complete the Huai River Diversion Project. The funds for the construction of the new Grand Canal will be raised by the Jiangsu Provincial Government through other means and completed in the short term.

The representatives took the 9:00 AM Beijing-Shanghai express train to leave Shanghai and embark on the journey. The representatives who came to see them off all returned. It is learned that the factory representatives plan to parade and promote the exhibition after arriving in Wuxi, so that all sectors of Wuxi will pay attention to it.

To Prevent Reactionary Elements from Causing Trouble

According to Da Gong News Agency, September 1 is the anniversary of the Second Congress of the Communist Party held in Chicago, USA. American Female Aviator Bland Quietly Leaves Shanghai 158

Because She Did Not Find a Chinese Female Comrade

According to the Mainland News Agency, American female aviator Bland arrived in Shanghai on August 11 to seek a Chinese female aviator to establish a branch of the Ninety-Nines club. However, she failed to meet a single Chinese or foreign female aviator in Shanghai, so she quietly boarded the President Adams ship and left for Hong Kong. The lady told a Mainland News Agency reporter, "I did not expect to find many female aviators when I came to Shanghai, but I thought I could find a few. I knew that China had banned private flying, but I had heard of one or two Chinese female aviators when I was in the United States. But after arriving in Shanghai, it seemed that no one knew about them. I have traveled to several countries and have never failed to find a female aviator in a country. This is the first time. I have found them in Cuba, Jamaica, Panama, Hawaii, and Japan. I am going to South China now, and perhaps I can find a few." According to the report, the lady left New York a year ago for a world tour and will need another two years to complete her journey.

Lake Society Petitions the National Government to Promote Domestic Textile Formal Wear 162

Memorial Weeks and Ceremonies Require Formal Wear

People's Weddings, Funerals, Celebrations, and Gatherings Must Also Wear Them

The style of formal wear in China has long been stipulated by the Ministry of Interior, but few people follow it. Lake Society of this city is aware that domestic textiles have been declining in recent years, and that people's clothing is uneven, and that they only favor foreign goods. Therefore, Shen Tianxin, the director of the Society's Industrial Department, proposed to petition the National Government, the Military Affairs Commission, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Interior to issue a nationwide order that everyone should follow the prescribed formal wear and use domestic goods to make their clothes proper, promote domestic production, and regulate the people's clothing. The original text is as follows: "We believe that the key to governing a country is to cultivate oneself before managing one's family, and the method of transforming the people is to guide them with virtue and especially to enrich them with etiquette. Clothing that is not correct is a disaster for the body, and frugality and simplicity are the essence of etiquette. Our China has always been known as a land of etiquette and righteousness, and the clothing of the upper kingdom has long shocked foreign customs. Since the reform of the government, the Ministry of Interior has clearly stipulated the formal dress, formal hat, ceremonial dress, and ceremonial hat, and has attached illustrations to explain them, and has ordered all levels of the country to comply with them. Even if they comply with them, they are often not domestic goods. For example, when people have happy events, they wear either Chinese clothes, Western suits, or square jackets and long robes, but the colors are mottled, or short clothes and narrow sleeves, but the forms are strange. They even flaunt their novelty and buy goods from abroad to compete with each other. They ignore the laws and regulations and are ridiculed by friendly countries. Nothing is worse than this. The difference between humans and animals lies in the ability to understand etiquette and love the country. If they cannot understand etiquette, then strange clothes and strange attire will lose the respect of sight. If they do not know how to love the country, then barbarian cloth and Japanese robes will show the overflow of power. In order to implement the new life, our Society intends to petition all provinces to order their subordinates that in the future, (1) when holding memorial weeks and important meetings, and (2) when there are happy or funeral events, they should all wear formal wear, and civil servants, except for the military police, should set an example and order that domestic goods be used for all silk, wool, and cotton textiles used in making formal wear. In this way, clothing can be regulated, and the promotion of textiles will prevent profits from flowing out. The matter concerns the national system and the people's livelihood, and it is reasonable to submit a document for review and implementation, which is of public convenience. Respectfully presented by Chen Qicai, Chairman of the Lake Society Committee."

Special Survey Record of National Products Industry 165

(2) Electric Light Bulb Industry

In recent years, the promotion of the electrical industry in our country has progressed rapidly, leading to an increasing demand for electrical appliances. Electric light bulbs, as daily necessities in electrical appliances, have the widest application and are most closely related to people's lives. In recent years, the concept of Chinese people loving and using national products has deepened, and most people are happy to use domestically produced light bulbs. Therefore, they have been able to compete with foreign goods. Within a few years, it is hoped that foreign goods will be completely eliminated. Recently, we interviewed Mr. Hu Xiyuan, the general manager of the leading Yabu Er Electrical Factory in this industry, to learn about the general situation of the industry. The electric light bulb originally came from abroad and was sold at a very high price. Later, the Chinese Yabu Er Electrical Factory took over the business from foreigners and specialized in manufacturing domestically produced electric light bulbs. After their products came out, foreign goods were greatly impacted. In order to avoid Chinese tariffs and reduce transportation costs, foreign merchants then set up factories in our country to manufacture. At the same time, Chinese people, seeing that there was profit to be made, also set up light bulb factories one after another. However, due to a lack of both financial resources and talent, countless factories were established but closed down shortly after. It is very difficult to run an electric light bulb factory. First, there must be technicians with rich experience in chemistry and machinery. Second, there must be skilled workers with long-term training. Third, there must be sufficient capital. If any of these three is lacking, even with millions in capital, it is likely to fail easily. This type of light bulb uses glass as its main material. The manufacturing process requires forty-two connection operations. If the technology is not sophisticated and the workers lack experience, not only will the products not be marketable, but the daily losses, both obvious and hidden, will account for more than twice the total expenses. For example, in the 10th year of the Republic, the Guang Ya factory, run by a certain Cantonese person, spent all of its 300,000 yuan in capital in fifteen months and completely went bankrupt. In addition, there were countless factories that were poorly managed and suffered losses and shutdowns. The Yabu Er factory, which has a longer history and better results, is a clear example. With a small amount of capital, it produces a large quantity. In the past ten years, it has experienced countless hardships and suffered countless setbacks. Currently, its capital has reached 500,000 yuan. The dedication of the authorities is by no means a matter of luck. Recently, due to the decline in the market and the fierce competition in the industry, the situation has become more intense. However, the factory's foundation is solid, all the workers have been trained for a long time, and the technology has become very skilled. Recently, it has spared no effort in recruiting electrical talent. If it can add the latest machinery and expand testing equipment, it will be able to make greater progress. The industry initially had no association. Last year, due to the impact of foreign goods dumping, an association was organized. Its name is the "Shanghai Electrical Manufacturing Industry Association," which includes other electrical manufacturing factories. According to a survey in the 22nd year of the Republic, there were a total of sixteen national product factories in this city specializing in the manufacture of electric light bulbs. Two have now closed, leaving only fourteen. This year, of the fourteen, five have suspended operations, leaving only nine operating normally. The production capacity of these nine factories is 14,875,000 light bulbs per year, of which the output of the Yabu Er factory is 6,875,000 light bulbs. The other factories together produce 8,000,000 light bulbs. Last year's sales of electric light bulbs were approximately 27,000,000 light bulbs, of which foreign goods accounted for one-quarter, counterfeit goods accounted for slightly less than two-quarters, and national products accounted for slightly more than one-quarter, with actual sales totaling 9,500,000 light bulbs. The Yabu Er factory alone accounted for half of this number. The above quantities are not entirely sold in Shanghai alone. However, most of the electric light bulbs in various provinces and cities are purchased from Shanghai. After the September 18th Incident, the sales of domestic light bulbs in North China decreased sharply. The ones that replaced them were naturally mostly foreign goods. This depends on the Chinese people's ability to distinguish and not be deceived. Among the industry, it is especially important to be united and consistent, fully improve technically, and cooperate hand in hand. Do not manufacture crudely and recklessly, and do not fight each other, so as not to lead to failure (Tianran).

National Postal Workers' Representatives Go to Beijing as the Postal Conference Approaches 166

Eleven Important Proposals

Submitted to the Congress for Discussion

The Ministry of Communications will convene a National Postal Conference, which will open in Beijing on September 1st. The National Postal Workers' Union considers this conference to be of great importance to the future development of the postal service and has paid close attention to it. It has specially sent representatives Zhang Kechang, Zhu Xuefan, Zhao Shusheng, Shi Yitang, Huang Gongfu, Shi Jikuan, and others to Beijing, and they are carrying eleven proposals for postal reform: (1) The case of merging the Savings and Remittance Bureau into the Postal General Administration has been passed by the Legislative Yuan and should be merged by the Ministry of Communications in accordance with the law to strengthen the postal foundation. (2) The co-establishment of postal and telecommunications services should be based on the principle of not harming the postal economy, as advocated by the authorities. (3) The postal economy has shown a trend of turning to residence year by year, and the treatment of postal workers should be improved within the possible range. The salary and holiday systems for all levels should be appropriately improved. (4) The postal economy has suffered losses due to aviation subsidies in recent years, and aviation subsidies should be stopped immediately. (5) The positions of Deputy Director-General and below of the Postal General Administration should be filled by current postal personnel. (6) Regarding the improvement of bureau affairs, this union proposes: 1. Develop the parcel business. 2. Build or repair local bureaus. 3. Improve sanitation facilities. 4. Improve postal delivery methods. Please ask the congress to decide on the implementation. (7) Please abolish the personnel knowledge examination and advanced examination. (8) Hold personnel selection examinations to gather talent. (9) The postal economy should be genuinely transparent. (10) Revise the postal outline. (11) Improve the clothing of field employees in various places. These proposals will be submitted to the congress for discussion.

Retired Accountant of Hongjitang Pharmacy Accused of Embezzlement 174

Witness Also Implicated, Handed Over to Police for Investigation

Xu Shifang, from Qingjiang, manager and accountant of Hongjitang Pharmacy at 1059 Dongxi Huade Road, resigned in June of this year and founded Houde Tang Pharmacy at 932 on the same road. Later, shareholder Wu Genrong, a local, discovered that during Xu's tenure at the store, from September of the 20th year of the Republic to June of this year, he had embezzled 600 yuan of deposits from his wife's younger sister, Gao Linshi. He reported this to the Huishan Police Station, which sent investigator Li Hongsheng to arrest Xu and bring him to the First Special District Court. Xu denied the charges. He was ordered to post 1,000 yuan bail pending trial. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Zehan visited the Third Criminal Court for a continued hearing. Li Zhishan, the attorney for the Municipal Council, stated that during the adjournment, the wife of shareholder Xu Yongxiang filed a report with the police station, claiming that she also had 1,400 yuan of deposits in December of the 20th year of the Republic, which were handed over to the defendant and his friend, Liang Zixiang, from Ningbo, but no deposit book was given. However, in the following year and at the end of the 22nd year, the defendant paid her annual interest of 1%, or 140 yuan for every 100 yuan, and attached two red receipts. There is no record of this deposit in Hongjitang's accounts. The police station is investigating this case, so no additional charges have been filed yet. The two interest red receipts were presented for inspection. Subsequently, shareholder Xu Yongxiang reported that the 600 yuan deposit of Gao Linshi was entirely handled by the defendant, and the deposit book seal was also stamped by him, and had nothing to do with him. Furthermore, witness Liang Zixiang testified that he worked at Wanhe Pharmacy on Xian Gua Street outside the South City and was a friend of the defendant. At the time when he left Hongjitang, there was a contract stating that the two shareholders were willing to pay a reward of 1,600 yuan, and that he was no longer responsible for any accounts after that. Witness Jie Minghan's statement was the same. The defendant was questioned, but he firmly denied the charges. Regarding Xu Yongxiang's wife's 1,400 yuan, he said it was a loan. He remained evasive about the rest. Municipal Council attorney Li Zhishan stated that witness Liang Zixiang had a significant relationship with the 1,400 yuan deposit book, and requested the court to allow the police station to take him away for investigation. Judge Wu approved the request and adjourned the case for further review.

Deadline for Land Tax in Shanghai County Remains Three Months 175

Order Issued by Jiangsu Finance Department to Comply

The first installment of land price tax for the 22nd year in Shanghai County was opened for collection at the counters on the first of this month. Subsequently, the county government, seeing that Article 2 of the Jiangsu Province Regulations on Late Payment Penalties for Land Tax stipulated that the tax collection period was limited to two months, but the county had already opened for collection in advance according to the old three-month deadline, immediately made corrections and reported to the Jiangsu Finance Department for instructions. The department responded with a telegram from Director Zhao stating: "After investigation, the new regulations on late payment penalties, limiting the period to two months, only apply to Zhenjiang, Jiangyin, Yixing, Liyang, Jiading, Kunshan, and Baoshan counties. The remaining counties should continue to follow the old regulations. Please be informed." After receiving the telegram, County Magistrate Pan, in addition to informing the tax collection office, issued a notice to the public yesterday, asking all businesses to be informed that the collection period for the first installment of land price tax for the 23rd year in this county will continue to follow the old regulations, with a limit of three months. Late payment penalties will be levied after the deadline.

Crackdown on Sleeping Outdoors in the French Concession 177

The police authorities of the French Concession in this city have found that since the arrival of autumn, the weather has been hot. Every evening, people seeking coolness in vegetable markets or on the sidewalks of various roads carry bedding and sleep everywhere, obstructing traffic and greatly hindering sanitation. Several days ago, the authorities issued an order to the chiefs of the police stations to dispatch detectives to drive them away in sections every late night. However, these people waited until the detectives left and then lay down on the spot again. Therefore, last night, a large number of detectives were dispatched to drive several trucks and arrest them in different directions. Those who were caught were sent to the respective police stations in the trucks to be temporarily detained until dawn, when they were released home. They were informed that they would not be allowed to sleep in the vegetable markets or on the sidewalks in the future, in order to maintain hygiene and avoid the spread of disease.

Taihu Lake Basin Water Conservancy Association Investigates Drought Conditions 183

The Shanghai County Government has received instructions from the Taihu Lake Basin Water Conservancy Committee, stating that this year, various counties in the Taihu Lake Basin have experienced a lack of rain during the monsoon season, resulting in severe drought and low water levels. The Building of a Dam for Irrigation in Gaoqiao Causes Misunderstanding Among Villagers, Leading to Repercussions 184

Local Gentry Step in to Mediate

A Disturbance is Finally Settled

This year, due to severe drought and scarce rainfall, farmers everywhere are extremely anxious. The Lingjia Muqiao West Ni Jiaxiang River channel in Gaoqiao Town, Songnan, has not been dredged for many years, and the river mud is silted up, preventing seawater from flowing smoothly. The municipal authorities, out of concern for the people's livelihood, have started to build a dam in Ni Jiaxiang and ordered the Dredging Bureau to use a large water pump to pump water for farmers to irrigate their farmland as much as possible. Unexpectedly, as the dam was nearing completion, it was opposed by the general villagers, who believed that the construction of this dam would be greatly detrimental to the farmers in the future. They mistakenly blamed Lu Guixiang for initiating it, leading to groups of people going to the Lu family to question him. Their actions were rude and clumsy. Mr. Lu repeatedly advised and explained the good intentions of the authorities in considering the people's situation, asking them not to misunderstand. However, the ignorant people did not believe him deeply. Lu had no choice but to lead the villagers to Ling Yunzhai's place in order to escape. However, the villagers continued to make noise and cause trouble even after arriving at the Ling family. Mr. Ling felt that he had been unjustly slandered and that Lu Guixiang had caused this. He decided to file a lawsuit against Lu Guixiang to clear his name. Subsequently, Mr. Zhong Youliang and other local gentry from Gaoqiao stepped in to mediate. Lu apologized to Ling in writing and guaranteed that similar incidents would not happen again in the future. Therefore, the disturbance over the building of the dam was finally settled.

Inland Waterways Shipping Nearing Complete Shutdown 186

Inland Navigation Bureau Requests Relief from Zhejiang Construction Department

The Shanghai inland waterways steamships have been greatly impacted this year. Those that have suspended operations due to the drought already account for 98% of the total, but there are still several steamships struggling to operate on the Huzhou-Hangzhou lines. However, with the continuous receding of the river water in recent days, they will also have to suspend operations. All steamship companies have suffered significant losses, with the Inland Navigation Bureau suffering the most severe damage. It has already submitted a request for relief to the Zhejiang Construction Department, and the current situation is recorded as follows:

Routes Already Suspended 187

Since the drought and shallow water levels, the Shanghai inland waterways steamships that have been unable to operate and have suspended service include the Shenxia Line, Gandang Line, Suhang Line, Changli Line, Xili Line, and others. The number of short-distance steamships that have suspended service is even more numerous to mention. Many of the steamships that have suspended service are stranded halfway and have been unable to return to Shanghai. The bottoms of the ships are now high and dry on the riverbanks, and the iron plates have grown moss. The barges and towing companies have also suffered the same fate, and the hulls of the ships have gradually been damaged. In places like Yixing River, the bottom mud has become as hard as cement. This is truly a catastrophe for the inland waterways steamships.

Shanghai to Hangzhou Line 188

Of all the inland waterways steamships, only the Shanghai-Huzhou and Hangzhou lines are still struggling to operate. On the Huzhou line, the water has also receded greatly in the past few days, and the steamships cannot reach directly. The entire line is divided into three sections and is pulled by manpower. The Shanghai-Hangzhou line has been even more difficult to navigate in the past ten days. It is still possible to operate from Shanghai to the vicinity of Zhenze, but afterwards, it is necessary to change to shallow-water steamships. Even then, it is difficult for shallow-water steamships to pass through, and it is necessary to use manpower to pull large ropes for rescue.

Imminent Shutdown 189

Yesterday, a person from the inland waterways steamship company said that if it does not rain, the river water in the interior of Jiangsu and Zhejiang will be completely dry within two months, and the small steamships on the Hangzhou-Huzhou-Xili lines, which can be relied upon to pass through boats, will not be able to be pulled and towed after another month. The complete shutdown of inland waterway transportation in the two provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang is imminent. This is an unprecedented situation in the past sixty years.

Request for Relief 190

The Inland Navigation Bureau is the largest operator of inland waterways steamships in Shanghai, with a total of eleven routes and more than sixty steamships and company ships. Now, due to droughts in various places, the services have been suspended one after another. Only the Huzhou-Hangzhou lines are struggling to operate. The crew members of the suspended ships are still being paid as usual. It is now estimated that the loss in revenue is more than 30,000 yuan, plus the expenses, and there is no end in sight. The bureau is leased to the Zhejiang Construction Department. Within four years, it has suffered four losses due to floods, military disasters, wars, and droughts. It has now appealed to the provincial government for relief, citing the example of Zhejiang Province's relief for drought disasters, due to the bureau's steamships suffering a major drought and completely suspending operations. The submission has been made and is awaiting approval.

The hospital reported the incident to the police, who transferred the body to the coroner's office for examination and notified the family. When his parents received the news, they rushed to the scene, but it was too late. They were overwhelmed with grief as they stroked his body, which was heartbreaking to hear.

Magic Trick Swindle of a Huge Sum 191

A Loud Bang, Flames Erupted

Five Thousand Dollars Turned to Ashes

Shen Baochang, the younger brother of Shen Baohe, a local resident living at No. 130 Jiuxiao Chang in the city, is currently working as a salesman in the printing industry. Recently, a friend introduced him to Pei Zhongying, an executive of a certain large company, who wanted to order a large quantity of printed materials. Baochang thought he had received a huge business deal, so he tried his best to please him and became very close to him. At first, they discussed samples and prices, and Pei Zhongying deliberately pretended to be an amateur and allowed him to open an account. Unexpectedly, a week ago, Pei Zhongying suddenly discussed something with Shen Baochang. He said that he had a Western magician who could transform banknotes in the same way. For example, a 1,000 yuan banknote could be turned into 2,000 yuan in ten minutes. He had asked the Westerner to transform 5,000 yuan for him as a capital for doing business, but he could not borrow this huge sum of money at the moment. He wanted to ask for help to raise 5,000 yuan, which would only take ten minutes, and he would return it and pay interest of 200 yuan. He also said that for the sake of mutual trust, Shen Baochang should monitor the scene to avoid any negligence. Baochang himself did not have this huge sum of money, but because they were on good terms and it was not convenient to refuse, he turned to his brother Shen Baohe for help and borrowed the money in various ways, raising 5,000 yuan. He then accompanied Pei Zhongying to the Western magician's place at a certain number on Huanlong Road in the French Concession and placed the silver banknotes on the table. Baochang watched closely and saw the Westerner perform magic. Unexpectedly, in less than five minutes, there was a loud bang, and the 5,000 yuan banknotes on the table were burned to ashes. Baochang immediately asked Pei Zhongying to return the 5,000 yuan banknotes. Pei said that the disaster was caused by improper performance, and that now that things had come to this, he could only write a temporary IOU and try to raise the money to repay him. Baochang had no choice but to take the IOU back to his brother. Baohe said that he had been cheated by a magic trick and that he should quickly negotiate with the Pei surname. However, he did not know the Pei surname's residence. Unexpectedly, one afternoon a few days ago, Shen Baochang passed by Laobeimen and encountered Pei Zhongying and his mistress Chen Wangshi. He immediately called the police and they were detained at the first precinct of the second district for investigation. After Shen, the precinct chief, learned that the case involved a magic trick swindle of a huge sum of money, he ordered them to be sent to the General Bureau for legal action.

Woman Had Another Love and Abandoned Him

The Concubine's Lover Was Angry and Ruthlessly Laid His Hands On Her

Wu Guizhen, also known as Yang 囡, a woman from Suzhou, was 22 years old and had a certain degree of beauty and a very romantic nature. She had an affair with Wang A'si from Chongming. First, the Western police chief reported the investigation process, and said that the deceased and Wang A'si had fought three times before. Also, according to Liu Ziyu, the deceased, a native of Funing, rented the back building of his house on the 20th of this month. Wang A'si came to visit at 9:00 AM yesterday morning, but the deceased had gone out to buy vegetables. He came again twice, but did not meet her. Later, he did not know how he killed her. After Guo learned of the situation, he ordered that the deceased, Wu Guizhen, female, was indeed killed by being slashed in the head with an ax before her death. The suspect, Wang A'si, should be strictly arrested by the police station and brought to justice. The body was handed over to Pushan Villa for collection.

Chinese Merchants' Public Bus Company Should Still Divert to Zhongxing Road 199

Letter from the Shanghai North Eight Roads Business Association

To: Chinese Merchants' Public Bus Company

The Shanghai North Eight Roads Business Association sent a letter yesterday to the Zhabei Chinese Merchants' Public Bus Company, requesting that the company divert the No. 3 special express bus back to Zhongxing Road in order to maintain the city's economy and facilitate travel. The original letter is transcribed below: "To whom it may concern: The development of local enterprises and the progress of culture must rely on transportation as a hub. There is more than one way to transport, but it depends on the needs of the locality. In Shanghai, in terms of the current situation, the Zhejiang Road intersection in the south is the center of Shanghai's transportation. Therefore, the business of the three companies (Sincere, Wing On, Sun Sun) is booming. Places such as Caojiadu and Xujiahui in western Shanghai are far away from the three companies, but they are relying on convenient transportation to flourish. Our Zhabei area has almost no transportation. Although it is close to the three companies, transportation and culture are still blocked, which is a great sigh. The Datong Road and Zhongxing Road area in the north connects to the concession in the south, Liuhang in the north, Wusong in the east, and Zhenru in the west. In recent years, there have been many commercial factories, vegetable markets, hotels, restaurants, and theaters. Municipal facilities are becoming more and more complete, but transportation is inconvenient, and travelers regard it as a danger, which affects the city's economy. In June of this year, your company diverted the special express bus from Qiujiang Road via Zhongxing Road to Dayang Bridge. After only a month, the owners along the road were very active. Some planned to build houses, and some bought land. Transportation is very important to the city's economy. Unexpectedly, your company suddenly changed the route to Jiaotong Road, which greatly disappointed the merchants and people. For the sake of local business development, we hereby send this letter, hoping that your company will forward it to the Municipal Government and the Public Works Bureau, and divert the special express bus back to Zhongxing Road in order to facilitate transportation and promote the city's economy. We will be very grateful."

Shanghai Municipal National Medicine Association Stipulates Regulations for Establishing Medical Colleges 205

The Shanghai Municipal National Medicine Association, in order to gather the opinions of various medical groups in this city to solve medical and pharmaceutical affairs at any time, specially invited representatives from each group to form a special committee. The association appointed He Yunsheng, Lu Shi'e, and Yan Cangshan as special committee members. The Shanghai Municipal National Medicine Association nominated Guo Boliang, Jiang Wenfang, and Shen Xinjiu. The Shenzhou National Medicine Association nominated Gu Weichuan, Xiao Tuian, and Cheng Diren. The China National Medicine Association nominated Yao Yunjiang, Huang Peisheng, and Bao Juxiang as representatives. The first special committee meeting was held last night to discuss the formulation of regulations for establishing medical colleges, which was submitted by the joint meeting of supervisors and directors for unification and improvement. All of the above committee members were present, and He Yunsheng was elected as chairman and Jiang Wenfang as recorder. First, He Yunsheng reported the purpose of the meeting, and then the regulations for establishing medical colleges were discussed and approved and revised as follows: Regulations for Establishing Medical Colleges (A) Organization: (1) There should be a board of directors consisting of seven or more people as the highest authority. (2) The board of directors should elect a president and vice president to preside over everything. (3) The president should hire one director of academic affairs to preside over academic affairs, and hire six professors to teach various subjects. (4) The president should hire one director of training to preside over training affairs. (5) The president should hire one director of general affairs to preside over general affairs. (6) The president should hire several dormitory supervisors to manage the dormitories. (7) Each group should be in charge of various matters and have group meetings or joint meetings to resolve various matters. Each director cannot hold concurrent positions. (B) Equipment: (1) There should be a fund of 50,000 yuan. (2) There should be at least three classrooms that can accommodate more than 50 people. (3) There should be a library equipped with books, human models, and drug specimens. (4) There should be a hall, dormitory, dining room, reception room, and various offices. (5) There should be a clinical practice place. (6) There should be sports facilities. (C) Academic Year: (1) Students must complete four grades to graduate. Each grade must have two semesters. Each semester must have 16 weeks or more of classes. (2) Students in the first and second grades should focus on reading. Students in the third and fourth grades should either read or practice. (D) Curriculum: (1) New students must have graduated from high school or have an equivalent level. Transfer students must have a considerable level of medical knowledge. (2) At least the following courses must be taught during the academic year: Party Principles, Chinese, Medical Classics, Materia Medica, Pathology, Injury Basis, Febrile Diseases, Pulse Studies, Medical History, General Theory of Medicine, Miscellaneous Diseases, Gynecology, Pediatrics, Surgery, Otolaryngology, Traumatology, Medicine, Medical Theories, Physiology, Infectious Diseases, Diagnostics, Prescriptions, and Chinese medical books should be used as a blueprint as much as possible. (3) Examinations must be held monthly, periodically, and annually. A graduation examination must be held at the end of four years. Only those with excellent results can be issued a diploma, and a certificate conforming to the provisions of these regulations will be issued by the association.
