Grain Sales to the North Cease, Flour Market Weakens 280

Yesterday in the flour market, after trading opened in the morning, all months showed signs of weakness. Overseas wheat quotations showed declines of approximately 0.12 candareens in Chicago and 0.05 to 0.06 candareens in Canada. At the open, market participants were influenced by continuous rains in the interior and the halt in sales to the north, as well as consecutive days of falling overseas wheat prices. As a result, confidence was extremely weak, and prices fell by about 0.02 candareens compared to the previous day. However, short covering caused a recovery of 0.01 candareens by the close. When trading reopened in the afternoon, all months showed further declines. Reports indicated that Australian wheat prices had also returned to 5.60 yuan. Local factories' flour sales were unexpectedly weak. It was claimed that the disruption of river transport in various locations had naturally halted flour demand, and that even Tianjin and other regions were experiencing inability to purchase due to rural bankruptcy. Consequently, there were rumors of deliveries, and longs were forced to liquidate. Distant months also declined sharply as major factories actively sold. Given the weak physical sales, further declines are likely. As a result, the current month fell by 0.055 candareens compared to the previous day, September fell by 0.0525 candareens, October fell by 0.0575 candareens, November fell by 0.05 candareens, December fell by 0.045 candareens, and January fell by 0.0375 candareens.

Imported Wheat Prices Gradually Becoming Favorable 281

Resulting in the Decline of [Futures] Wheat

Yesterday, after the wheat market opened in the morning, all nearby and distant months fell uniformly, and selling pressure was intense. Confidence was extremely weak due to further declines in imported wheat prices, falling by 0.05 to 0.06 candareens to 0.12 candareens, and a return of Australian wheat prices to 5.60 yuan. The market price gradually approached that of Shanghai, but factories were uninterested in imported wheat due to sluggish flour sales. Even spot wheat was being withheld in anticipation of lower prices. Because of the decline in spot imported wheat prices, marked wheat saw aggressive selling by hoarders, leading to declines month after month. The market was even weaker in the afternoon. By the close, September was down 0.07 candareens, October was down 0.09 candareens, November was down 0.1 candareens, December was down 0.08 candareens, and January was down 0.12 candareens. Factory demand for spot wheat was very sluggish, with intentions to wait for further price declines. As a result, there were no transactions for the entire day.

High-Quality White Rice Hoarded by Merchants 282

Unwilling to Sell at the Price Ceiling

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, only thirteen or fourteen shipments arrived from various regions (totaling over 2,000 dan). Sales were sluggish, resulting in further price declines of several cents to about a dime for thick-grain and late-season rice. Only Du Yangjian and Yinyuan remained stable due to low supply. Special-grade rice experienced price declines of over 0.2 candareens due to plentiful arrivals from various locations and limited sales. The factories were specifically offering 11.8 yuan.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, fourteen or fifteen shipments arrived from various regions along the river, but sales were slow for all varieties. High-quality white rice was unavailable for sale because merchants were unwilling to sell at the price ceiling of 13.5 yuan. The market saw price declines of 0.2 to 0.3 candareens for white rice and thin rice, and 0.1 candareens for Baiyuan new premium-grade rice. Yangdujian also trended weak. Arrivals of Dongxin glutinous rice were relatively strong, but sales were weak, with prices falling by 0.2 candareens.

Zhejiang Rice Prices Plunge After Rainfall 283

Declines Range from 0.3 to 0.6 Candareens

Yesterday, the market for imported early rice was uniformly down, with light trading, weak confidence, and the likelihood of further declines. At the opening yesterday, prices for all grades of imported rice were expected to decline because customers from Hangzhou, Shaoxing, and other areas of Zhejiang province had received reports of rainfall in their regions and were returning home. Physical demand immediately halted. Even brokers acting as agents were mostly watching the market. Total purchases from interior merchants were only about 1,000 bags. Local merchants bought opportunistically, but only purchased a little over 1,000 bags in total. As a result, small-grain rice fell by 0.5 to 0.6 candareens, machine-milled rice fell by 0.4 to 0.5 candareens, and brown rice also fell by 0.3 to 0.4 candareens. Road shipments also fell by 0.4 candareens. Dealers in imported rice warehouses were watching the market, and Saigon rice had already arrived at the port, with road shipments also expected to arrive soon. Physical buyers and interior customers were mostly selling their futures contracts. Backdoor trading in Saigon rice had already fallen by 0.1 to 0.2 candareens. There were few sellers of small-grain rice, so prices were temporarily stable.

New Sesame from Yangzhou Falls Another 0.5 Yuan 284

The Situation for New and Old Soybeans is Not Good

Yesterday, the price of new sesame from Yangzhou fell another 0.5 yuan, opening at 6.1 yuan, with 70 bags traded, purchased by local merchants. The weakness of the new sesame market was caused by the large amount of arrivals when old sesame was being turned over, which were all high-quality. New sesame itself is inferior to other sesame, so demand is low. In addition, arrivals continue, so in just one week since its listing, its price has fallen by 1.4 yuan. The market for new and old yellow soybeans is not good. Sales of new soybeans were less than 500 bags, so prices continued to fall. Old soybeans were not selling at the sesame oil factories, and there was no market revival.

Dried Goods, Old Longan Experiences a Major Price Drop 285

The existing inventory of old longan was extremely low. Based on previous years' sales, it was expected that it would not last until the new crop. However, sales this summer were significantly reduced due to drought, with only sporadic transactions. As a result, new longan has already arrived, but the old crop has not yet been sold. Therefore, the market price has plummeted. The current market price for ordinary large-kernel longan, previously offered at around 60 yuan, is now only 36 to 37 yuan, a decrease of 23 to 24 yuan. Those with large inventories are mostly suffering losses.

Silk and Tea: Overseas Silk Sales Show No Improvement 286

Prices for Lyon Raw Silk are Extremely Low. Japan had abundant spring and summer silkworm harvests this year, leading to a sharp increase in silk production. Japanese silk merchants are aggressively dumping cheap silk on European and American markets. Recently, prices for Lyon raw silk have been extremely low. Zhong Shenhai Cup brand is only 39.5 francs per kilo, and special grade Eight Arrows brand is only 42 francs (both 13/15 denier), which is 12 to 13 francs lower than Chinese silk from Shanghai white factories. As a result, sales of factory silk in France remain difficult.

Few Hangzhou-Shaoxing Cocoon Waste Shipments to Shanghai. Silk weaving factories in the interior are starting to weave winter semi-silk fabrics, leading to a sharp increase in demand for cocoon waste for long spinning. There are few shipments of Hangzhou-Shaoxing cocoon waste. This month, a total of only 73 pieces were shipped from the Communist region.

The Foreign Silk Market Remains Weak. Recently, overseas markets and sales of raw silk from factories have shown no improvement. Shanghai Chinese silk merchants report that the prices offered by European and American white silk factories are still more than 100 yuan below cost, resulting in huge losses. They are watching the market and not selling. Yesterday, only Xinfu and others imported 20 bales of white factory silk and 10 bales of white silk yarn, with prices remaining weak.

Needle and Special Grade Tea Sales to France Improve 287

Yesterday, the local foreign tea market saw resumed purchases of green tea, such as needle and special grade tea, by British firms such as Jinlong, Xiehe, and Fushi, due to demand from Morocco. Total sales for the city were over 800 boxes. High-grade teas sold for 40 to 51 yuan, and low-grade teas sold for 16 to 22 yuan, both down 2 to 3 yuan from before. As for fine eyebrow green tea, European firms only made sporadic purchases, and there was no significant market progress. There were also no major transactions for Gongxi and Gongzhu teas. It is difficult to be optimistic about the green tea market.

Metal: American Galvanized Iron Arrives in a Flood, Sales are Sluggish 288

Due to the suspension of export shipments, business in this street for American galvanized iron is scarce, so the market is unusually weak and prices are secretly declining. Currently, 31-gauge is estimated at 1.57 yuan per sheet, 28-gauge is estimated at 14.85 yuan per picul, 26-gauge is estimated at 13.8 yuan, and 24-gauge is estimated at 12.85 yuan, about 0.1 yuan lower than before. Only a little over a hundred bundles have been offered for sale in the market in recent days.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Commentary

Concern for People's Food and Rural Relief 289

— Chen

This year the weather is scorching, with a prolonged drought, especially severe in the provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, and Jiangxi. Fields are cracked, and rice crops are withered, indicating a disaster. Shanghai rice prices have therefore risen repeatedly. What used to be six or seven yuan per picul is now selling for twelve or thirteen yuan per picul, almost doubling. However, the population of over three million still needs to eat, and they can only sigh as rice prices rise, handing over stacks of silver dollars to rice shops. Thus, everywhere under the scorching sun, countless farmers are weeping as they sweat to bail water while watching the withered rice crops. Workers in the city are groaning under the heavy burden of rising rice prices. But those wealthy merchants who purchased and hoarded rice cheaply last year under the guise of a "bumper harvest" are sitting by electric fans, squinting and smiling happily at the influx of wealth flowing their way.

There's no need to "hold a pipa halfway and cover your face" and hide anything. To be honest, in times of drought and disaster, the sweat and tears of the broad masses are the source of nourishment for these wealthy merchants who sit high and speculate. "Concern for people's food" has become a good opportunity for rice merchants to get rich. But nobody admits it, always offering explanations and excuses. The issue of whether or not Shanghai should buy imported rice is a farce of this kind.

Since Shanghai rice prices soared, the soybean and rice industry has suggested ordering 500,000 piculs of imported rice and requesting the government to waive import duties. This matter has attracted serious attention from all parties. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the Grains Guild, and the Inland Rice Merchants Association of Changsha have all held meetings, issued declarations, and sent telegrams, arguing that there is no need to purchase imported rice and requesting the central government to strictly prohibit it. Those who advocate purchasing imported rice say: disaster has struck, people's food is at risk, rice prices are soaring, the people cannot bear the heavy burden, and imported rice should be purchased duty-free to suppress rice prices and help people's food. And this is also presented as a great patriotic and benevolent principle.

For members of the same industry to engage in mutual attacks, is it truly out of a dispute over the issue of "concern for people's food and rural relief"? This is somewhat doubtful. Those who have already hoarded a lot of rice, or inland rice merchants who own grain themselves, naturally rejoice at the rise in rice prices and hope they will continue to rise. The import of rice hinders their attempt to raise market prices. They shout that purchasing imported rice destroys the countryside and affects the national economy, without seeing that they are not reducing rice prices to "maintain people's food." As for those who advocate purchasing imported rice, they see the high rice prices and the potential for profit, and they are eager to obtain tariff exemptions to make a big deal. So they are seizing the opportunity, using "suppressing rice prices and helping people's food" as a pretext to purchase imported rice as much as possible. The recent transaction of 160,000 piculs of Saigon rice is a case in point.

In fact, are those who oppose the purchase of imported rice truly helping the countryside? Not to mention that farmers generally sell all their rice at low prices after the autumn harvest due to the pressure of rents, debts, and taxes. The fact that rice prices are being hoarded and raised to obtain high profits shows their intentions. And are those who purchase imported rice truly concerned about people's food and suppressing rice prices? We see that the recent transaction of 160,000 piculs itself indicates that they are waiting for a good price to sell, which also shows their true intentions and has nothing to do with "helping people's food." This is the cleverness of 20th-century people. It is clear that everyone is taking advantage of this disaster to "loot a burning house," but they still put on a lot of pretenses. But those with discerning eyes can always recognize that their so-called "concern for people's food and rural relief" is purely a way to beautify the "business principles" of profiting from disaster!

On "Literary Heritage" and "Foreign Eight-legged Essays" 290

— Mingtang

I admire the abilities of the "Literature" group of people.

I recently saw a copy of "Literature" Volume 2, Number 6, "Special Issue on the Study of Chinese Literature." At the beginning were two short articles discussing the issue of Chinese literary heritage. Their opinion was that Chinese literary heritage is worth organizing. Chinese literary heritage has countless grains of gold hidden in a desert: this gold is just waiting for us to unearth it. We need to sort through the countless Chinese literary heritages, pick out what we need (meaning like this, because the original text is not on hand, unable to quote the original sentence). I felt very strange at the time. What we currently need seems to be literature that can express contradictions (contradictions in objective reality) and resolve contradictions. But at this time, "Literature" is perversely proposing to organize Chinese literary heritage and accept Chinese literary heritage. What does this mean? So at that time, I casually wrote a short commentary, which was published in the "Commentary" column of this publication. My opinion is: Chinese literary heritage, indeed, is worth organizing. But now is not the time for us to leisurely organize Chinese literary heritage and accept Chinese literary heritage, right? So my conclusion is: the "Literature" proposal to organize Chinese literary heritage and accept Chinese literary heritage is just a more clever way to escape reality and escape contradictions. There will be no other meaning besides this. At that time, I wrote that article, originally not expecting anyone to "particularly value" it, and the "Literature" group would not "particularly value" my so-called "foreign eight-legged essay" that was not worth "particularly valuing." Unexpectedly, "Literature" actually superficially "did not particularly value" but valued my so-called "foreign eight-legged essay" that was not worth "particularly valuing." In "Literature" Volume 3, Number 2, I found an article signed by "Feng," titled ""Literary Heritage" and "Foreign Eight-legged Essays"." They launched a good attack on my article. His conclusion is: my article is a complete "foreign eight-legged essay"; secondly, the reason why they proposed organizing Chinese literary heritage and accepting Chinese literary heritage is said to be in order to "throw bombs into the old Chinese literature camp"! and carry out a "disinfection" movement for Chinese literature. In this way, their proposal to organize Chinese literary heritage and accept Chinese literary heritage has become a very "respectable" and meaningful work that is anti-"infatuation with old literature" and guides it to the road forward. This is a very clever "setting of words." However, everyone with discerning eyes can see it. Is this the fact? Alas, even a so-called "three-foot-tall child" would probably find it a little hard to believe. (To be continued)

Random Notes from the Sickbed, Part 3 291

— Red Tea

In the past, out of my own interest, I dabbled in old poetry, calligraphy, painting, and seal carving. Now, bored in my illness, I want to resume my old life, naturally aiming at leisure, but I am also afraid of exertion, which would be harmful to my sick body. Now let me write a little about the things of the past to quench my thirst by looking at plums.

In elementary school, my writing was very bad. When I was about to graduate, I still couldn't write better than a third-grade student. My father often said so to my face, but there was no way to write well.

Later, I happened to pull out a volume of Huang Shangu's calligraphy from the Sanxi Tang Calligraphy Collection and found it very pleasing. Especially the large-character "Poem Sent to My Forty-ninth Nephew." So I took a brush and copied it several times, and then practiced it again the next day. After several times, I showed it to a gentleman who studied calligraphy and painting. It was a real surprise! He actually said it was very good. Not only did he say it was good, but he also wrote a sentence in red ink on the paper: "There is much of the feeling of the B鶴銘 inscription." I went back and looked at the "B鶴銘 inscription" and it was indeed very much in line with it. So I diligently practiced the B鶴銘 inscription. The gentleman even came every day to correct it. It is true that calligraphy requires a hundred days of effort. After two months, it was actually quite presentable. The gentleman also wrote on the paper some sentences such as "The dots have the momentum of mountains collapsing stones, and the strokes have the beauty of clouds stretching for thousands of miles." This made me even happier. However, I had no foundation at all. From the beginning, I studied characters that relied purely on spirit. Although the brushwork was similar, I was ultimately unable to give my characters a complete composition. As a result, each character looked good individually, but the whole composition looked very bad, because the B鶴銘 inscription was already a remnant stele, with no connection between the characters or between the lines. At this time, I knew the danger, so I tried to learn Zhang Menglong and others, but to no avail. Later, I saw a copy of Huang Shangu's 在文 and Mu Yan Lu Gong's Sacrifice 文 drafts and found them very pleasing, so I took them to copy, but the accumulated habits were too deep and I could no longer completely correct them.

As for painting, I have always liked it. In the third grade of elementary school, I was able to paint Huang Zhong and Zhou Yu almost as well as the figures in the Illustrated Romance of the Three Kingdoms. While practicing the B鶴銘 inscription, I began to paint landscapes. At that time, I listened to the gentleman and learned Wang Hui, the leader of the Four Wangs, because his Zhongfeng Pi Ma wrinkles were the least flawed. But my gentleman was learning Ni Gaoshi's folded-belt wrinkles. Unintentionally, I followed the gentleman again and also learned the folded belt. This slowed my painting progress a lot. Later, I saw the works of Huang Heshanqiao and felt that his momentum was more imposing than Wang Hui, so I abandoned Ni Wang to learn from him. This made things worse and worse. Not long after, I flipped through the works of the monk Shitao on the easel and felt, "He is truly my teacher!" So I abandoned Huang Heshanqiao to learn from him. Although my temperament was similar and I was able to grasp his general idea, it was ultimately not good.

While learning to paint landscapes, I also saw the seal manual of Wanbai Shanren (Deng Shiru). I was excited for a moment and took out old iron brushes and stone seals to carve randomly from the drawer. At that time, I first wrote the characters on the stone seal with a brush, and then carved according to the characters. Later, I learned that carving this way was wrong, so I carved randomly with my hand. At this time, I was looking at too many miscellaneous seal manuals, so my seal carving also suffered from the same problem as my calligraphy and painting.

As for the last three years, because I have been running around, I haven't held a brush for a long time. What's more, at this time of carnage and bloodshed, new art is waiting to be learned and developed. At this time, talking about ancient seal carving, calligraphy, and painting is really about being fascinated by a skeleton. But in my case, the accumulated habits have not been eliminated. Especially when I have nothing to do while sick, I unconsciously think of the pleasures of that time.

Finally, among modern young people of about my age, there are probably very few who have dabbled in these things. This is their good fortune, because I myself have indeed been immersed in old learning for too long and too widely, and my ideas have been greatly influenced by it. But what can I do?

Autumn Courtyard 292

— Gazing Tower

Early autumn has arrived, and while the pleasant weather brings a sense of comfort, a layer of melancholy inevitably covers the sorrowful heart. "Don't be so sentimental, winter and spring will follow autumn." Sometimes, I try to reason this way, hoping to dispel the shadows in my heart, but the shadows continue to grow longer with the passage of time. I foresee that before long, these shadows will engulf my entire heart once again.

The sweltering heat of summer makes people feel lazy and weary, longing day and night for the autumn breeze to dissipate the heat. In anticipation, autumn is almost like a merciful God, bringing almost nothing but blessings. It seems only autumn can save all living beings, lifting sinners from purgatory one by one.

Indeed, autumn has arrived as hoped. The shadows of the elm trees are thinly reflected on the window first, and the flowers and grass soon turn withered and yellow. The night breeze blows, bringing quiet, coolness, and freshness. We should be grateful for autumn, but instead, my heart sinks into deep sorrow.

We know that autumn is just one season of the year, like spring and winter, neither particularly joyful nor particularly sad. But people are so clever and yet so pedantic. When spring arrives, they are all smiles, seeking and cherishing the spring. But for autumn, they only grieve for it, even weep for it. The god of autumn and the messenger of spring are equally happy or equally without any intention of causing joy or sorrow. They are merely the changes of time, treating us people equally. But we people divide them into one lovable and one hateful.

In my childhood innocence, autumn was not so different from other seasons. In spring, we could make willow balls from willow branches; in summer, we could catch cicadas. In autumn, there were crickets chirping, enticing us to find them. All seasons were filled with joy and happiness. But as I grew older, even the Spring Festival, which I used to love, gradually lost its original joy. I only felt that another year had passed and I was another year older. In autumn, I gradually began to feel unhappy when I heard the wind and rain. People say I've grown up, but I say I've suffered more. Because the joy of catching crickets in those days is not only completely gone, but even hearing the chirping of autumn insects makes me feel sad. The heart of a happy childhood has long been buried deep by frequent sorrows.

Now, having lived a few more years in this world, looking at the lonely long sky in the autumn courtyard, my mood is as faint as the chirping of the little insects in front of the steps.

A person in the autumn realm is about to enter the autumn realm of life!

Within the Autumn Banana Scars 293

— Mu Yin

The green banana leaves, exposed to long hours of sunlight, dew, wind, and rain, bear scars that intertwine with various hidden states of anger, love, leisure, and sorrow – the elusive emotions of a maiden. They reveal elements akin to ice and charcoal. Who would have thought that the harsh stripping of this crisp autumn season would destroy its long-held plans for expansion, leaving only a few breaths of abandoned children for us to grieve with?

It feels fortunate not to have withered before the fragrant osmanthus, and to be able to enjoy the sight of newly fertilized chrysanthemums. But the beauty of the eastern fence, and the stirring of the hero's spirit, pierce its weak life, storing the intention of recovery. Indeed, although it is only a few pieces of fragmented green, it never forgets its efforts in imagining the opportunities for its future.

The wind blows in gusts. The sound of leaves rustling echoes from the four neighbors. The peeling of the autumn paulownia, accompanied by the tearing of the decaying banana leaves, forms a mutual tune. The weak grass beneath its tall stem, for the hope of survival, is willing to sacrifice the precious moisture of the thick dew, begging it to preserve its only remaining strength to shelter it.

For the trust of its kind, for the survival of life, it has no choice but to struggle with tears. The self-defensive battle with autumn! It will completely sacrifice its beauty, and that is because it is driven by anger.

The autumn moon pours out its crystal-clear color, as if it will tie together all spirits and become the universe's deep silence. The cold cicada weeps! It feels the coldness of the autumn dew. It, the banana, under this moon where falling paulownia flowers break the silence, only has the movement within the stillness to accompany it through the long night, lamenting its encounter with fate.

Page 21

Beneath the Volcano 294

— Zang Fei

The quiet evening of July, with its chilling drizzle, weighed down on every depressed heart. I walked aimlessly on the slippery road, a shadow swaying beside me under the dim streetlights. A hand reached out from behind.

"What are you doing?" I grabbed a skinny arm! He opened his startled eyes and said in a pleading tone, "Good lady! Let me go! I'm hungry, I need to eat!"

Looking at that innocent face, my hand loosened, and I sadly watched the shadow swallowed by the darkness: "He's only that young!"

Then, the voice "I need to eat" echoed stubbornly in my ears. This was familiar to me, and many emaciated faces floated before my eyes: I saw them grabbing withered yellow leaves and greedily putting them in their mouths; I saw them frantically eating the bloody child dragged back from the railroad tracks – it was reported in the newspaper last year, I forget where – parents, because of hunger and unable to bear killing their children themselves, put them on the railroad tracks, let them be crushed to death, and then dragged them back. I even saw them ending their vibrant lives with their own hands.

A bright light shone on me, and I had reached a busy road. Nothing was left behind except that innocent face, those startled eyes.

Cars rushed by frantically, and suddenly a thought burst into my mind: "If he had been born into a wealthy family, wouldn't he have had a bright and rosy childhood? But now, what has deprived them of their youth? What has deprived them of their right to exist?"

I walked silently to the school, saw the magnificent school gate, and thought of China's lack of talent, and of the wanderers drifting on the streets.

The rain was still falling, and the sky was dark with no stars.

Amateur Mailbox

Recovery of Loan Association Funds 295

— Editor

Editor:

I have a difficult problem and request your help in resolving it. The situation is as follows:

About forty years ago, my father left a loan association slip with a relative, claiming it was my father's handwriting. (Whether it is actually his handwriting is questionable, as I have never seen my father's handwriting.) At that time, I was not even born, and my mother had not yet married.

My father married my mother over thirty years ago, and then I was born. Three years later, my father unfortunately passed away, leaving my mother and me to depend on each other for the next twenty years, without ever knowing about this matter.

Yesterday, the relative, who had not been in contact with my family for decades, suddenly came to my house to demand the so-called loan association funds and said many unpleasant things, threatening to use the law to recover the debt. I felt deeply insulted and could hardly bear it. Just as I was at a loss, I suddenly remembered that your newspaper has an amateur correspondence column that can help us with all kinds of problems. I dare to present the details of this matter and ask you to answer the following questions. I await your reply with the utmost anticipation.

Yours sincerely, Zhen

The questions are as follows:

(1) In law, can a loan association slip be legally binding?

(2) If the loan association slip is indeed my father's handwriting, am I responsible for repayment?

(3) If a loan certificate from the Guangxu era can still be valid now, can this forty-year-old loan association slip also be valid?

(4) If a lawsuit unfortunately occurs, what should I do?

Answer: Your letter was received a long time ago, but I have delayed in replying because there are too many letters in backlog. I am not familiar with the term "loan association slip" you mentioned and am not sure if it means "IOU." However, since the other party intends to rely on this document to request the return of the debt, they undoubtedly possess a "right to claim." According to the current Civil Code, "The right to claim is extinguished if not exercised within fifteen years." The loan association funds have been outstanding for more than forty years and have not been demanded from you. Therefore, the right to demand payment has certainly been lost. Therefore, you don't need to worry. Whether the loan association funds exist or not, whether the slip is genuine or fake, it is no longer a matter of concern as the statute of limitations has expired. As for the other party wanting to file a lawsuit, either they have no legal knowledge at all, or they are trying to scare you because they think you are ignorant. You don't need to be afraid.

Novel

A Major Event in Five Family Town (9) 296

— Zhang Yiping

"Old Master Wu is..."

"Old Master will make a fair judgment..."

"Old Master Wu..."

The expected praises rang in Rich Gonggong's ears like thunder. Old Master Wu stroked his neat beard with a smile. He felt he had completed a satisfying masterpiece today.

Zhang Defu opened his mouth, he had won. At the same time, seeing Old Master Wu's proud hint, he hurriedly pushed Rich Sheng's shoulder and said:

"Thank you, Gonggong Wu, for coming in this hot weather!"

"It's nothing, nothing," Old Master Wu said indifferently, "Rich Sheng often comes to my house with your mother, don't become strangers within the family."

"We will, Gonggong Wu," Zhang Defu rushed to answer.

Old Master Wu stood up from the grand chair, fanning himself with a goose feather fan, and straightened his clothes. "Okay?" As if seeking everyone's consent, "We can go."

Rich Gonggong seemed to wake up from a dream. He was listening intently to the cursing from inside, and for a moment, he forgot to say a few polite words. Instead, Rich Sheng said:

"Gonggong Wu, wait until the sun goes down before leaving."

"Good boy! Someone is waiting for me at the Xinglong Tea House."

Old Master Wu took his hand and walked outside all the way, saying, "Would you like to come to my house to play?"

A group of people followed them out, with Rich Gonggong walking at the back with a sullen face.

The two black gate doors opened, and the neighbors who were poking their heads out quickly dodged aside. The sedan chair carriers carried the sedan chairs from under the shade of the trees to the front of the door. Everyone thanked Old Master Wu before getting into their respective sedan chairs and returning home. Rich Gonggong, however, stared blankly at the departing sedan chair shadows as if he had lost his soul, sighed deeply, turned around, and slammed the gate shut with hatred.

Many pairs of puzzled eyes were cast on the black gate doors. They never understood what the major event was that had brought the Zhang Defu family together today.

The sun slowly moved west from the gate doors, and the cicadas still chirped loudly in the distance. (The End)

Shen Bao Local Supplement Movie Special

Lilian Harvey's Last Effort 297

Will Return to Europe If Unsuccessful

Excessive Publicity Can Cause Repercussions

It is strange that Lilian Harvey, the petite and graceful actress whom our Shanghai audiences generally like, seems to have some difficulty gaining a foothold in Hollywood. From various Hollywood film magazines, it seems that they do not express deep regret or sympathy for her impending failure. Moreover, since the general audiences or film critics in the United States do not overemphasize content and ideology as much as we do in Shanghai, this is indeed a difficult thing to understand. (However, one magazine said: "If we let her leave, it would be an unforgivable sin for Hollywood.") It is said that she recently filmed a movie (Serenade). If she does not succeed exceptionally in this film, she will no longer make a living in Hollywood. This may be a bold prediction, but it is something she told people herself. She said, "If this film is not a special success, then Hollywood and I are finished!"

Since seeing her first Shanghai screening of "Congress Dances," her beautiful image has been deeply imprinted in our hearts. Up until the latest "I am Suzanne," our feelings about her have been very good. Among them, there are also several of her French language films, which also have considerable appeal. She has not been in Hollywood for long, but in the Fox Company, although Janet Gaynor – also a female star whom most Shanghai audiences like to watch – is in fact occupying the Queen's position, she has already become the first red star. Last year, she filmed three films in total, and the business was not bad, but Lilian herself was very dissatisfied with her work. You know, this young lady is outspoken. She thinks what she says; she says what she does. Since she herself is not satisfied with her own work, she is unwilling to continue doing it in a half-hearted manner. She said, "It's either the best, or the worst. It's either a great success, or it's better to leave America forever."

When a reporter went to visit her, she actually started complaining to herself. She said: "I have failed here. I know it myself. According to my contract, I still have to film two more movies after finishing this one, but I feel that (Serenade) is my last movie. If the result is just average, then there is no need to try anymore. I should just go home." Lilian's home is a fashionable villa in the French Riviera. So she is going back to Europe to make movies. She also said, "Audiences spend money to seek entertainment, you cannot force them to accept a star they don't like. I have tried running to the movie theaters myself to take their criticism. I think they are not stupid, they have good judgment, they can appreciate real entertainment. But in Europe, they like me very much!" Indeed, Lilian Harvey is the most popular female star in Europe. Her "Congress Dances" filmed in Berlin was welcomed everywhere, and the Fox Company's invitation for her to come to America was also accompanied by special and extensive publicity.

However, according to Lilian herself, this expanded publicity was her fatal wound. Before Lilian arrived in Hollywood, Fox had already begun to hype her up. People who read the newspapers read about her itinerary every day, as if a foreign queen was coming to visit. When she arrived in Hollywood, forty large trunks of luggage and a cloud of servants followed her, as well as a silver-white "imported" car. The Fox Company also arranged for her a exquisitely decorated residence on the company grounds, and all the furnishings and decorations were carefully selected and expensive to please her. But now Lilian says, "These have all harmed me! I did not demand so many luxurious things. That kind of publicity is not what I like. On the contrary, it has caused a backlash in the minds of the audience. When the public heard so many nice things, they thought a miracle in the world had appeared. When they took a look and there was nothing particularly amazing, they returned disappointed. Otherwise, they could have liked me very much. The publicity was too much!" Lilian is a talented woman who has received higher education, so her words are very thought-provoking.

Film Reviews

Review of "The Whirlpool of Life" 298

— Ling He

Whirlpool｜｜Grand Theatre

Regardless of the cold reception this film may have received in China, we must admit that it is a better production from Columbia Pictures and a worthwhile work among American films. However, the reason for its unpopularity may be that the name Jack Holt does not resonate deeply with the general Chinese audience.

Speaking of the film itself, although it still contains many flaws, on the whole, it does not disappoint us too much. We believe that when a person tries desperately to rise from adverse circumstances, but society does not allow his aspirations, the fallen can only fall further, and finally end in a tragic death. Therefore, Lincoln's struggles in the whirlpool, his efforts to save himself, his good conscience, his willingness to sacrifice himself for the happiness of his wife and daughter, his tragic suicide, and his painstaking efforts never being understood by his wife even after his death – in these aspects, the playwright evokes great sympathy from the audience, which is undoubtedly a victory.

From this perspective, the playwright firmly grasped human emotions as the main method, and completed a sentimental ethical tragedy. However, precisely because of this, he treats this human tragedy entirely as an idealistic exhortation. Thus, he believes that a fallen person, if he has a conscience, should sacrifice himself to ensure the happiness of his wife and daughter, even to the point of suicide. This does not involve a rigorous analysis and dissection of society, and relying on individual good and evil to address a serious part of social problems naturally offers no way to find a solution. This demand is not excessive for filmmakers, but it is very difficult for most American playwrights.

To reiterate, up to this point, the playwright's and even the director's methods of expression still move us. (1) When Lincoln is sentenced to twenty years in prison, the scene of the couple crying while facing each other across the iron bars reminds us of the moment before Lincoln killed the man, when the couple were playfully and slightly sentimentally toying with their wedding rings, as well as the embrace at the time of the sentencing and the painful separation – that profound emotion can only be achieved by film. (2) In prison, Lincoln sadly begins to endure those long years. But his cellmate desperately tries to escape, only to jump from a high place into the water, and amidst the dense gunfire, we only see countless bubbles and waves emerging from the dark water, and that life ends just like that. (3) Lincoln is released from prison after serving his full term, and the two large iron doors close heavily behind him. He begins to gain freedom, looks up at the blue sky with infinite hope. He spent half his life in prison, and now his hair is gray, and the world has changed a lot. The new-style cars cannot help but arouse his curiosity. (4) He is a kind-hearted man. After protecting his daughter's flesh and blood, he resolves not to rescue his accomplices anymore. But society cannot tolerate him, and when forced to, he has to kill that lawyer. Then he burns his wife's photo, gazing at her face as it is destroyed in the fire. This makes us think of the first time he asked his daughter, "How is your mother? Is she happy?" and accepting the photo of his already wealthy wife joyfully in the bar late at night. Then the daughter and the old friend hear a gunshot, and this man who has been steadfast and unwilling to fall all his life ends here. Here, the director matches both gunshots with close-ups of the daughter and the old friend's faces. Especially the last shot, the degree of emotion we feel seeing the faces of the daughter and the old friend is definitely something that ordinary, vulgar directors cannot achieve. (5) A small death cannot evoke deep sympathy in the human world. In the quiet night, although the radio broadcasts his death as news, it is just a very ordinary thing, and his death cannot break the deathly silence. The wife quietly embroiders flowers next to him, and she never understood his life at all. An ordinary life, an ordinary death, everything passes by ordinarily... We cannot deny that this sentimental atmosphere has indeed victoriously shaken our sorrow.

After seeing "The Fugitive," and then seeing "The Whirlpool of Life," there are many similarities. If we only talk about the method of expression, then the former is very successful in terms of tension and stimulation, while the latter, with many natural and lively jokes, makes the plot not feel dull at all, and the balancing of sadness and joy is Roy William Neill's specialty. If the former makes us excited and sad, and the latter makes us sentimental and melancholic, then it is fully achieved.

The actors, of course, Jack Holt, the protagonist, performs the best, and the rest of the cast are also very suitable for their roles.

New Trends in American Cinema 299

— Dong Lin

Recently, there are two new trends in the American film industry, that is, they will produce a large number of literary films and classical films.

1. Literary Films: MGM will produce Dickens's "David Copperfield." United Artists will produce Tolstoy's "Resurrection," starring Anna Sten and Fredric March, directed probably by Mamoulian. And Dumas's "The Count of Monte Cristo," and Jack London's "The Call of the Wild." Warner Bros. will produce Sinclair Lewis's "Babbitt." And Universal will produce Alan Poe's "The Raven," and so on.

2. Classical Films: Because MGM's "Treasure Island" was very successful, all companies are competing to produce classical films. It is said that Warner Bros. has already begun to produce "Captain Blood." 20th Century Fox has also successfully produced "The Affairs of Cellini," starring Fredric March and Constance Bennett. As for RKO, it will also have Katharine Hepburn star in a film about a queen.

Submission Guidelines for "Shen Bao" Film Supplement 300

This publication is a film publication that assists cultural promotion and art. All foreign manuscripts are welcome and generously compensated once published.

Once a manuscript is published and paid, the copyright belongs to "Shen Bao."

The language of this publication is mainly modern vernacular Chinese, and new-style punctuation must be used. If the submission is a translation, the original work should be attached. Avoid mixing in English as much as possible.

Do not write on both sides of the paper or horizontally, and do not use pencil.

Due to limited space, the writing should be concise. Each submission should be around 500 words.

Each submission must be stamped with a seal, otherwise it will not be compensated.

This publication is not responsible for preserving or returning texts, photographs, etc., unless otherwise stated in advance and return postage is included.

Submissions that are submitted to multiple publications, plagiarized, or copied from explanations will not be compensated once discovered.

Film Novel

The Struggle to Love and Obtain a Child (Doctor Monica) (11) 301

— Ti Yun

Anna ran outside and hurriedly made a phone call to Manley in Ironton. She told the maid not to make tea and just give her some water. She drank a sip of water and, with a determined look on her face, went out the gate, jumped into a car, and went straight to Ironton. When she arrived in Ironton, she straightforwardly told Manley about the matter. She told Manley that on the night the child was born, Monica knew that the child was John's, and now Monica was going to leave John forever because of this. At first, when Manley heard that Monica was going to leave John, a look of hope appeared on her face. She thought that after Monica left, John would belong to her alone. Anna saw her face, understood her meaning, and told her, "If John still loves you, then of course it's different, but John doesn't love you anymore. I'm telling you the truth." The radiance on Manley's face immediately dissipated. She hesitated and said, "Oh. That's for the best. Because..." She paused again, because this lie was too far from the truth, making it almost impossible for her to speak, "I don't love him anymore either." Anna knew her thoughts and comforted her with pity, "There are really too many women who are misled by love. Why should you be sad?" Manley said, "I will make everything right tomorrow." The next afternoon, Monica returned home from outside, and the maid hurriedly opened the door, telling her that Miss Manley had sent a child. She told Monica, "The nanny who sent the child said that you understand everything." Monica said, "But I don't understand. Where is Mr. Brandon?" Emma said, "The master hasn't returned yet." Monica sighed, and her heart was much calmer. She walked into her bedroom, looking at the child sleeping in the bed. Monica looked at the child with curious eyes. Emma then sent over a letter, which the nanny had left. Monica opened the letter and read it, her breathing quickened, and her face changed. Emma asked, "Is it important?" Monica revealed a flustered look and said, "It's not important. This child is being fostered here by a friend." Emma said, "Aren't you leaving tonight?" Monica said, "I'm afraid my plan has to change a bit." As she spoke, she lowered her head, brought it close to the child's face, and thought of Manley, grateful to her for arranging everything so well. At this moment, the door outside rang. She knew that John had returned, and she quickly put the child down and ran outside. John walked in and said sadly to Monica, "In a few hours, this place will be different." Monica stammered, "John, I have something to tell you. I... I don't know how you'll deal with it." John looked at her inexplicably, waiting for her to continue, but the phone rang urgently, interrupting Monica's words. The voice on the phone was Anna's. She asked with a crying voice, "Monica, have you seen the newspaper?" Monica said, "No. What's the matter?" Anna said, "Manley took her own plane and flew towards the Atlantic Ocean. She only brought a few hours' worth of gasoline..." Anna's voice choked and she couldn't continue. Monica was stunned. It turned out that she took the plane, not to go home as she said in the letter. She hung up the phone, stood with her back to John, trying to calm herself. John still asked, "Isn't she coming to see you off?" Monica said, "I'm going to see her in a while." John asked again, "What were you going to tell me just now?" Monica took his hand and led him to the bedroom, where he saw a child. He looked at Monica in surprise, speechless for a moment. Monica said, "I want to adopt her, okay?" John said, "Okay? Isn't that what we've been thinking about for a long time?" Monica looked at her, unable to tell whether it was joy or pain. She picked up the child and put her in John's arms, saying, "John, hold her, she's yours." She took a step back, tears streaming down her face. She looked out the window at the darkening sky, silently saying a tragic farewell to Manley. (The End)
